Genet. 51, 1411â1422 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d323e2180">28</a></sup>. A heat map of the interaction matrix of all pseudochromosomes was plotted with a resolution of 100âkb.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec14">Repetitive sequence and gene annotation</h3><p>Repetitive elements in the PI464715 genome assembly were identified based on a combination of homology-based and de novo approaches at both the protein and DNA levels. First, TRF v. 4.0.7<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Benson, G. Tandem repeats finder: a program to analyze DNA sequences. Nucleic Acids Res. 27, 573â580 (1999)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d323e2192">54</a></sup> was applied to identify the tandem repeats in the genome assembly. Then, TEs were identified using RepeatMasker v. 4.1.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Tempel, S. Using and understanding RepeatMasker. Methods Mol. Biol. 859, 29â51 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d323e2196">55</a></sup> and RepeatProteinMask (<a href="http://www.repeatmasker.org/">http://www.repeatmasker.org/</a>) with Repbase<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Lin, H. H., Liao, Y. C. &amp; Dutilh, B. E. Evaluation and validation of assembling corrected Pacbio long reads for microbial genome completion via hybrid approaches. PLoS ONE 10, e0144305 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d323e2207">51</a></sup> as the query library. Next, RepeatModeler v. 5.8.8<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Jurka, J. et al. Repbase update, a database of eukaryotic repetitive elements. Cytogenet. Genome Res. 110, 462â467 (2005)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d323e2211">56</a></sup> (<a href="http://www.repeatmaskerorg/">http://www.repeatmaskerorg/</a>) was used to construct a de novo repeat library for the identification of TEs that were not found in the Repbase library.</p><p>We predicted protein-coding genes using a combination of de novo prediction, homology-based prediction and transcriptome-based prediction. Augustus v. 3.3.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Stanke, M. et al. AUGUSTUS: ab initio prediction of alternative transcripts. Nucleic Acids Res. 34, 435â439 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d323e2226">57</a></sup>, GlimmerHMM v. 3.0.4<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Majoros, W. H., Pertea, M. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. TigrScan and GlimmerHMM: two open source ab initio eukaryotic gene-finders. Bioinformatics 20, 2878â2879 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d323e2230">58</a></sup>, Geneid v. 1.4.5<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Blanco, E., Parra, G. &amp; GuigÃ³, R. Using geneid to Identify Genes. Curr. Protoc. Bioinforma. 65, 56 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d323e2234">59</a></sup>, and Genscan<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="Birney, E., Clamp, M. &amp; Durbin, R. GeneWise and genomewise. Genome Res. 14, 988â995 (2004)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d323e2238">60</a></sup> software were used for de novo prediction. GeMoMa v. 1.3.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Keilwagen, J. et al. Using intron position conservation for homology-based gene prediction. Nucleic Acids Res. 44, e89 (2016)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d323e2242">61</a></sup> was used for homology prediction, with protein sequences from <i>M. truncatula, C. arietinum, G. max, P. vulgaris, P. persica</i> and <i>A. thaliana</i>. For transcriptome-based predictions, we first sequenced the RNA library generated from mixed stem, leaf and flower tissues, and the RNA-seq reads were assembled into transcripts using Trinity v. 2.1.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Grabherr, M. G. et al. Trinity: reconstructing a full-lentgh transcriptome without a genome from RNA-Seq data. Nat. Biotechnol. 29, 644â652 (2011)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d323e2253">62</a></sup> with default parameters. In addition, we mapped all the RNA-seq reads to the final assembled genome by PASA v. 2.1.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Haas, B. J. et al. Automated eukaryotic gene structure annotation using EVidenceModeler and the program to assemble spliced alignments. Genome Biol. 9, R7 (2008)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d323e2257">63</a></sup> to assess genome assembly quality. To annotate the noncoding RNAs, tRNAscan-SE v. 1.3.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Lowe, T. M. &amp; Eddy, S. R. tRNAscan-SE: a program for improved detection of transfer RNA genes in genomic sequence. Nucleic Acids Res. 25, 955â964 (1997)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d323e2261">64</a></sup> was applied for identifying tRNA genes with eukaryotic parameters. BLAST<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Camacho, C. et al. BLAST+: architecture and applications. BMC Bioinforma. 10, 421 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d323e2265">65</a></sup> was applied to search the rRNA sequences in the PI464715 genome assembly with default parameters. MiRNA and snRNA were identified using INFERNAL v. 1.1<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Nawrocki, E. P. &amp; Eddy, S. R. Infernal 1.1: 100-fold faster RNA homology searches. Bioinformatics 29, 2933â2935 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d323e2270">66</a></sup> software based on covariance models deposited in the Rfam v. 13.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Kalvari, I. et al. Rfam 13.0: shifting to a genome-centric resource for non-coding RNA families. Nucleic Acids Res. 46, 335â342 (2018)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d323e2274">67</a></sup> database.</p><p>Gene functions were annotated by performing BLAST<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Camacho, C. et al. BLAST+: architecture and applications. BMC Bioinforma. 10, 421 (2009)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d323e2281">65</a></sup> (<i>E-</i>valueââ¤â1e<sup>â5</sup>) searches against four protein databases, i.e., SwissProt, KOG, NR, and KEGG. The InterPro database with BLAST or InterProScan v. 4.8<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Jones, P. et al. InterProScan 5: genome-scale protein function classification. Bioinformatics 30, 1236â1240 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d323e2290">68</a></sup> was used to annotate the functions of protein-coding genes. UniProt and GO annotations were assigned for each protein based on the results of alignment.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec15">Gene families and phylogenetic analysis</h3><p>We used OrthoFinder v. 2.2.7<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Emms, D. M. &amp; Kelly, S. OrthoFinder: solving fundamental biases in whole genome comparisons dramatically improves orthogroup inference accuracy. Genome Biol. 16, 157 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d323e2303">69</a></sup> to identify the orthologous groups among 12 Leguminosae species (PI464715, <i>M. truncatula</i>, <i>T. pretense</i>, <i>P. sativum</i>, <i>C. arietimum</i>, <i>L. japonicus</i>, <i>P. vulgaris</i>, <i>G. max</i>, <i>C. cajan</i>, <i>L. angustifolius</i>, <i>A. duranensis</i>, <i>A. ipaensis</i>) and one rosid species (<i>A. thaliana</i>). We then extracted the single-copy orthologous genes from the orthologous clustering results. We used CAFÃ v. 2.2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Han, M. V., Thomas, G. W., Lugo-Martinez, J. &amp; Hahn, M. W. Estimating gene gain and loss rates in the presence of error in genome assembly and annotation using CAFE 3. Mol. Biol. Evol. 30, 1987â1997 (2013)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d323e2345">70</a></sup> software to identify the expanded and contracted gene families in the 13 species, which were further subjected to GO enrichment analysis. For phylogenetic analysis, we first used MAFFT to perform multiple alignments of protein sequences of single-copy orthologous genes with default parameters. Then, the protein sequence alignments were converted into codon alignments. Second, Gblocks v. 0.91<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Talavera, G. &amp; Castresana, J. Improvement of phylogenies after removing divergent and ambiguously aligned blocks from protein sequence alignments. Syst. Biol. 56, 564â577 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d323e2349">71</a></sup> was used to delete regions with poor alignment or large differences in the results of multiple sequence alignments. Finally, the codon alignment results of all single-copy orthologs were connected to form a supergene for phylogenetic analysis. RAxML v. 8.2.0<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Alexandros, S. RAxML version 8: a tool for phylogenetic analysis and post-analysis of large phylogenies. Bioinformatics 30, 9 (2014)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d323e2353">72</a></sup> was used to construct the phylogenetic tree. We calculated the average substitution rate along each branch and estimated species divergence time using r8s v. 1.81<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Sanderson, M. J. r8s: inferring absolute rates of molecular evolution and divergence times in the absence of a molecular clock. Bioinformatics 19, 301â302 (2003)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d323e2357">73</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec16">Gene collinearity and <i>K</i><sub>s</sub> analysis</h3><p>Syntenic blocks between PI464715 and the four monoploid genomes of alfalfa and <i>M. truncatula</i> ecotype Jemalong A17 were detected using MCScanX<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Wang, Y. et al. MCScanX: a toolkit for detection and evolutionary analysis of gene synteny and collinearity. Nucleic Acids Res. 40, 49 (2012)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d323e2377">74</a></sup>. The number of synonymous substitutions per synonymous site (<i>K</i><sub>s</sub>) on each branch was estimated using the codeml program in the PAML v. 4.0 package<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Yang, Z. PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol. Biol. Evol. 24, 1586â1591 (2007)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d323e2385">75</a></sup>, and the median <i>K</i><sub>s</sub> value was representative of the collinear blocks.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec17">Identification of resistance (<i>R</i>) genes</h3><p>We used both BLAST searches and the hidden Markov model (HMM) to obtain <i>R</i> genes in the PI464715 genome, the four monoploid genomes of alfalfa and <i>M. truncatula</i> genomes. All of the protein sequences annotated in these genomes were first searched by using the HMM profile of the NB-ARC domain (Pfam no. PF00931) in a hmmscan subprocess of HMMER 3.2.1 (<a href="http://hmmer.org/">http://hmmer.org/</a>). We used BLASTp to search the amino acid sequences of the NB-ARC domain against all annotated protein sequences in each genome. We merged all hits obtained from both analyses and removed the redundant hits. The sequences were further subjected to Pfam analysis and coiled-coil (CC) analysis to identify TIR, LRR, RPW8, zf-BED and CC domains. The method was similar to that used in a previous study<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="Lupas, A., Van Dyke, M. &amp; Stock, J. Predicting coiled coils from protein sequences. Science 252, 1162â1164 (1991)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d323e2419">76</a></sup>. We used paircoil2<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="McDonnell, A. V., Jiang, T., Keating, A. E. &amp; Berger, B. Paircoil2: improved prediction of coiled coils from sequence. Bioinformatics 22, 356â358 (2006)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d323e2423">77</a></sup> (the threshold value was set to 0.025) and coils software to identify CC domains.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec18">Identification and expression of lignin and cellulose biosynthesis genes</h3><p>To identify the genes involved in the lignin and cellulose biosynthesis pathways in PI464715, we used the genes listed in the diagram of lignin biosynthesis pathways in plants by Vanholme et al.<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="Vanholme, R., De Meester, B., Ralph, J. &amp; Boerjan, W. Lignin biosynthesis and its integration into metabolism. Curr. Opin. Biotechnol. 56, 230â239 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d323e2435">78</a></sup> and cellulose biosynthesis genes identified in the <i>A. thaliana</i> database as references<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 79" title="Lampugnani, E. R. et al. Cellulose synthesis-central components and their evolutionary relationships. Trends Plant Sci. 24, 402â412 (2019)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d323e2442">79</a></sup>. Then, the BLASTp algorithm and Pfam analysis were used to search our genome for homologs. The locations of all identified lignin and cellulose biosynthesis genes were marked on the eight chromosomes by MapChart v. 2.32 software<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Voorrips, R. E. MapChart: software for the graphical presentation of linkage maps and QTLs. J. Hered. 93, 77â78 (2002)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d323e2446">80</a></sup>.</p><p>To examine the expression of these lignin and cellulose biosynthesis-related genes, we carried out RNA sequencing of two tissues (i.e., leaf and stem, each with three replicates) through 2âÃâ151-bp paired-end libraries using an Illumina HiSeq 4000. Leaf and stem tissues were obtained from a voucher PI464715 plant. Raw Illumina reads of low quality (when the percentage of low-quality bases was over 50% in a read) and with unknown bases (&gt;10%) were filtered out to obtain clean reads. Then, the clean reads were mapped to the genome assembly using HISAT2 v. 2.0.4<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 81" title="Kim, D., Langmead, B. &amp; Salzberg, S. L. HISAT: a fast spliced aligner with low memory requirements. Nat. Methods 12, 357â360 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d323e2453">81</a></sup> with default parameters. Read alignments for transcripts in each sample were extracted using StringTie v. 1.2.3<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 82" title="Pertea, M. et al. StringTie enables improved reconstruction of a transcriptome from RNA-seq reads. Nat. Biotechnol. 33, 290â295 (2015)." href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d323e2457">82</a></sup>. The expression level of each gene was measured by transcripts per million (TPM) values estimated in StringTie.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="data-availability" data-title="Data availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="data-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="data-availability">Data availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="data-availability-content">
              
              <p>The whole-genome sequence data (including Illumina short reads, Nanopore long reads and Hi-C interaction reads), the final assembled genome and the transcriptomes of different tissues used in this study have been deposited in the NCBI database under BioProject ID PRJNA657344. The genome annotation information has been uploaded to Figshare.</p>

Q.-W.D. provided the seeds. Z.-P.L. helped plant the seeds. A. Li. and A. Liu. collected the materials, assembled the genome, and performed gene annotation, gene-family and evolutionary analyses. X.D. conducted resistance gene identification. M.Y., J.-Y.C, H.-Y.H, S.-D.W., and H.-Q.W. helped with data analyses. A.Li and G.-P.R. wrote the manuscript with help from N.S., Y.-Z.Y., and J.-Q.L. All authors read and approved the final version of the manuscript.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="corresponding-author">Corresponding authors</h3><p id="corresponding-author-list">Correspondence to
                <a id="corresp-c1" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7/email/correspondent/c1/new">Yong-Zhi Yang</a> or <a id="corresp-c2" rel="nofollow" href="/articles/s41438-020-00417-7/email/correspondent/c2/new">Guang-Peng Ren</a>.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="ethics" data-title="Ethics declarations"><div class="c-article-section" id="ethics-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="ethics">Ethics declarations</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="ethics-content">
              
                <h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="FPar1">Conflict of interest</h3>
                <p>The authors declare that they have no conflict of interest.</p>
